O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	To you, dear sons, I have completed this book which is the latter part of the science of medicine combined with its completeness. And I have done the end through its demonstrations and by its statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to my mind that I should complete this book with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the art of hands is practiced in our region and is unknown everywhere, it has been lost and discarded, and nothing remains from it except for small descriptions in books by the ancients that have been performed by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this, errors and vanity have come about, and minds are closed, and knowledge has become distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems I might revive this treatise altogether, according to the path of exposition, declaration and abbreviation;
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And will come together the forms of the metal cauteries and other tools of the operation with the adjustment of exposition and preparation of them, as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no good masters are found in our time, the art of medicine has been extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who intervenes to master in the art of anatomy, as Galen says, as long as he knows the measurement of the limbs, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and tendons, and the number of bones, and their movement and mobile and stationary veins, and the location of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And according to this says Hippocrates that without the tool we are little and with the work is less;
et meismement en l’art de main.	And similarly in the art of manual skills.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the introduction of this book that if someone doesn't know the things already mentioned, they might make mistakes and deceive people;
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	So often, many have entered this science and then abandoned their knowledge and experimentation.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	For I saw a madman looking at an abscess or neck of a woman, and cutting the arteries from her neck;
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	because so much blood flowed out that the woman died in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And I saw another madman treating a stone in an old man, and the stone was large;
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	so he took with him a piece of the bladder from it, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been summoned to extract, and saw the location of the disease and the size of the stone, and if they were well cut it would kill him.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another madman treating the Duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the breakage he got an injury;
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the surgeons full of ignorance caused the breakage on the wound in accordance with strong luck, and did not allow any medicine to reach the wound, and left it like that until the end.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	And he commands that she not loosen it at all;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And wait like that until the leg is completely healed and the feet came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I was summoned to come to him, and I hurried to come to release the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	And when I heard it dislocated so smoothly that he felt no pain at all.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But the entire corruption was already confirmed in his body or limb, and it could not be cured;
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	And the corruption continued to spread through the body until the limbs were completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And as for another instance where one abscess weakened another intertwined abscess, and then it inflamed due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humours, does not allow one to touch it with iron if it isn't in its entirety within what can be removed all that which has been corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, dear children, you need to know that the art of healing is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	This means, "it refers to," or "this is known as," where there's danger in multiple positions.
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it's necessary that you keep them in mind, so that the ignorant may not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take your tools in hand and treat your patients with both gentleness and firmness, and use the best method so that through the grace of God, you come to heal them and remain just;
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the unbearable diseases without cure;
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	And remove from those who make you doubt, and have faith in your skills so that you may come from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galiens states in some of his admonishments:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Never apply an inappropriate remedy for illness, lest you be called mad instead.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medicine-based cauteries, and they order the chapters from the head down to the stones;
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and descriptions of instruments, and the tools for cauterization, and everything else that is necessary for this task.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar matters.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	And these chapters are arranged and describe the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar matters;
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	And it is arranged concerning the position of the head up to the neck, and regarding the shapes of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we recall our work, it is fitting that I explain the quality of each aid and the harm of each constitution.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest word and subtlest science, and the secrets of response;
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	And many wise men spoke about this, and they agreed on it;
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	And their words satisfy me, for I fear the length of them.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that the cautery helps universally in any complexion where it has matter, for there are two complexions:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This means to know hot complexion with substance, and dry complexion with substance.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In the hot and dry complexion together having substance, they devised nothing and said that the cautery is a great help;
et li autre dirent le contraire:	And others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that the cautery is only beneficial for diseases that come from heat and drying.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For the nature of fire is so hot and should not be used to treat diseases that are caused by heat or drying;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	And it is those who say the opposite, that the cautery provides great assistance to hot and drying diseases that manifest in people's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the constitution of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in every case, do not intervene except for those who have tried it and know the chapter of cauteries by long usage, and understand the variety of people's complexions, and their conditions and causes of diseases, and the occurrences and span of treatment;
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	For other complexions we have none, just as in cold and wet illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all these matched and agreed with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that when assembled in fire, a cautery has secrets of healing arts, and it offers more benefit than a hot medical treatment.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come out except at the body part that is heated, and does not harm other parts if you do not name it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Medicines originating from one body part to another through circulation generate illnesses within the body.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	And by chance, it affects the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The fire, due to its height and the goodness of its quality, does not do this thing if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this I have found through experimentation and the length of my service and study in the art, and it aligns with the truth of things;
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	And for this reason I apologize for the length of my speech, because it does not please me to reveal the secret that lies with fire and the quality of the work, how it relieves diseases from bodies, as the philosopher demonstrates in his demonstration;
or le recevez en vos pensees.	Receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they decided on what times the cauterizations should be performed, and prescribed them carefully.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that the cautery is suitable in all circumstances, because the injuries caused come off easily with the help of the cautery;
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And indeed, if the cautery is for necessary pains that cannot wait until greater mischief befalls the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think like, silly child, as fools do;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	for the disease that is cured by cautery has no return;
et il le dient ensi;	and he says so;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not as they think, for cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion, dries the fluids which are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine because of its speed in increasing its power, and because of the virtue of its work and its authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And it is possible that a disease may occur at any time depending on the constitution of the patient and the location of the illness and its nature;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	And in him they assemble the excesses through acquisition of meats and similar things; if one does not administer cauterizations at this point or where there is little excess and moisture, such as with dense cauterization for pain, then that particular kind of pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	But this happens slightly.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And few people understand why cauterizations are called the ends of medicine; it is to be seen; and that's how it is.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	But they don't believe that cauterizations come after medicine; rather their understanding is false. Instead, in the realm of medicine, it is cauterizations which are considered as a final resort because whenever our treatments for any disease fail to produce results, then we administer cauterization and it becomes effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it is true that cauteries are at the end of medicine, not according to the understanding of those who misunderstand.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The old ones said that gold instruments' cauterizing tools are more effective than iron ones, and they mentioned this because of the quality of gold and the purity of its substance;
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they say that the blades of the cauterizing tool do not cause rotting, but this is not visible because I have tested it and found that it does become visible in some people;
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	And gold cauterizing tools are better than iron ones, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	And even so, when you heat gold tools, you may not know if they are hot by the color of the gold, and it cools off quite quickly;
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if they are heated too much;
si font au feu;	if it is put to the fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And thus there is enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason, we use our fire cautery that has been prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	So I have ordered this chapter on how to find the shoulder joint until this point, because it makes the search for it lighter.
dou cautere olivaire	with the olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The use of cautery is appropriate in cases of moisture and cold within the brain. There are two kinds done by reason of an illness called 'soda', and due to various humors descending from head to eyes, and ears, as well as from numerous dreams and toothache, and throat pain, and especially for all diseases coming from cold such as paralysis, soda (a type of stroke), apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be cleansed by a dissolving medicine altering the third or fourth part of the body, depending on what the properties and heat and habituation of the patient can bear;
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	Then resume the original function of the organ in the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit crossed between your hands, and place his hands on the back of his head;
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his second eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and leave where your thumbs arrive; if it bleeds from the cheek, heat the cautery called "olive" which has this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And mark its position on the body with ink, and guide your hand down and steady it little by little as you readjust.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	Then ease your hand slightly, and check the joint if you can see the bone has settled somewhat;
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	And if you don't see it, start using the cautery again until you see the bone as I have instructed;
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	After taking a small amount of salt, and put wet and soft cotton inside, place it on the joint, and let him rest for three days;
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	After place moist butter on the cotton.
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	And leave it until the charred part is removed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treat the wound with the ointment known as 'tetrafarmacition', until it heals properly.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And if one spoke of the old, saying that when more remains open the wound, more purges out;
et por ce si aide mues.	and because it moves with this assistance.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And it was said that one should leave the cauterization for so long that part of the bone gets burned, and then remove that which is burned from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And they say that one should apply the cautery until it heals, and press so hard on it as to make the opening as wide as a woman's pubic area when she gives birth; because this allows the body fluids to flow out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	And should we leave the wound open for a long time;
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	After that, one must clean and heal it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of using the cautery do not seem to be good for everything, except in cases where there is a way of fear;
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	And it seems to me that I should leave it as it is;
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	For the head of the shoulder is weakened by continuous exposure to nature, as we witness with other limbs;
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And even when the shoulder blade is weak by nature, and the first sign of a cautery is more healing and harsh for me, and with this I work together gathering health.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When there is chronic pain in the head and it lasts long, one should use remedies like herbs and pills that are called "cochines", and treatments for cleansing the head and ears and bandages;
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cautery as we have described before, and it is effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care that the head of the sick person is of strong constitution, and do not let it become too cold;
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Therefore, apply the cautery to that fire weapon a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After you have made the cautery on each hoof up to the bone, just like we explained before, and apply the cautery where the term 'knees' is called;
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and place them in the area where suction cups are used.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	And move your hand gently, so you do not see up to the bone:
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	Patients feel much more intense pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about it elsewhere;
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	And it is necessary that the cauterizations of the horns be more subtle than that which cauterizes the middle part of the head, and this is how:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery,
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When pain comes suddenly in part of the head, and extends the illness up to the eye, and the joints are treated with purging medicines, and other treatments that I have described for disease divisions, and nothing benefits from all this.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	So you do cauteries using two methods, namely with medicinal sweat and through fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	The medicine-based cauteries involve taking a spoonful of oil and applying it to the skin and covering it with I or II pieces of cloth; then heat it so that you can place the hot oil over the skin where the pain is located, allowing the oil to permeate through.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	And when it has been placed there, if you hold and press well and leave it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	And then the dislocation and treatment were removed after the use of garlic oil for twelve days or three;
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	Then place a butter poultice on it until pus begins to drain out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the ointment treatment as long as it remains clean;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	And if you see fit to use any of the burning medicines that I have written about, or the tenth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery operates in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery which is as follows:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head has the shape of a bell or it has one small curve, and in the middle there appears a little outline;
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	And place it at the painful head, and hold your hand and twist it a little gently, until half of the mustard seed is burned;
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And lift your hand so the artery doesn't burn, which has been exposed, and there is an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After placing cotton in the wound site, and let it sit for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then put moistened cotton in oil, and then treat the wound with ointment as long as it remains clean;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	And if you wish to cauterize this inflamed area with the fire cautery, which is called 'cultellare', all at once, and be careful not to cover the artery in this inflammation which isn't old.
de emigraine	Regarding the use of a fire cautery, instruct the patient to allow their hair to grow long and evenly; if they are pricking at their base, hold them steady so they don't move until they fully grow.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat inflammation as we have previously described in divisions of diseases, and if it doesn't improve, and you see that the cauterizations mentioned earlier in medicine and iron don't affect it, then it's necessary that you heat up the cautery which is called 'cultellare' until it becomes white;
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	And so when on the limb a line half the length of one's arm is drawn out, and you take hold with your hand once, and steady it so as not to cut the artery and do not ascend up to the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	And beware that the jaw remains quiet when one chews, and the tongue should only focus on remaining silent and avoid spasms occurring in the body, and beware of bleeding from the artery if it is cut, or if cutting has caused significant fear even to those who are unaware and inexperienced.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	And let the work be done according to my path;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to properly stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it occurs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you notice that these cauteries do not help with the illness, and the patient is suffering, apply them to the back as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals;
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	And if you observe, administer the cautery as we have said or in the chapter of artery extraction, with the cautery that has two blades;
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And indeed, these cauteries are better and more effective than others.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	The pain of the ear from both cold and heat
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes from cold in the ear, and we have applied solutive medicines and other treatments that we mentioned under division, and if the pains do not subside, then heat this cautery called "points", according to its form.
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After marking the entire area around the patient's ear or in both sides where pain is felt, and move away a little from the base of the ear after you have indicated its position.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and mark ten points around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment until it becomes healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	Tortures that should be treated by cautery can only include those that move with the blood, as we have mentioned in our discussions of diseases.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	And do not use cautery on symptoms that come from scarring and infection in the flesh.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you treat this symptom of blood-moving torture and the discharge of bodily fluids and purge from the head and gargling, if it doesn't work, then it should be that you apply three applications of cautery to the skin.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	One at the root of the ear, and another slightly beyond the temple, and the third at the adjustment of the two lips;
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	And place the cautery on the healthy part that opens, and apply it to the area above the ear's top until slightly over the corner of the head, and another on the temple as long as a finger.
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	And let the cautery burn until half of the thickness of the flesh is consumed;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	And it resembles the appearance of the scalpel that we showed before, but it is a bit more subtle. It is necessary for the knives to be a bit larger;
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	after treating the wound as I have described previously, until it heals properly.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and if it does not benefit, and the patient has a fever, then make four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	Two on the two horns of the head, and one under the head, and one where the neck is called "vessel" as we have said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach;
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	And make the treatment as we have said before.
de litargie	Of Liturgy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this illness, one must give the patient large grains and pill-like things to alleviate the head;
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	After removing the head's pain, place it on the back of the head with the tallow plaster that is written or treated for plasters;
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the way to apply the cautery:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	Do it as I have said if you do so.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If it is done like this, well done;
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	And if it isn't, you should apply three cautery treatments descending from the head to the neck, and leave two inches of space between each treatment.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	And treat it similarly to other cases, and if you find it properly setted, and the patient is suffering, then apply a fire cautery in the middle;
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it's needed, do so on the two horns as well, and treat until it becomes healthy;
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and may be that which is called 'olive fire' by the cauterization, as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	from the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of years and what we have mentioned previously;
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	After cleansing the head of the patient, then apply the fire on the head and on each horn, and later on three places near the neck spine;
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	And if you need more, and the horns are moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is persistent, then apply four fire cauterizations on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	And let him go until the most gentle wound is healed, and lift your hand;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the cure until it becomes clean, and use the cautery which is called "olivare" as we have already discussed.
de l’epilempsie	Regarding the application of a cautery with fire, instruct the afflicted to allow hair growth until it is long and even; and if they poke at their origins, restrain the eyes so that they do not move until they grow.
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use fire cautery if they are of the phlegmatic type, and it is necessary to first modify their diet with years' worth and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division where the diseases are large and suffer from medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it's a child who cannot endure the pain, make them gargle and chew frequently, often mixing their brain with good meats;
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	After the king's head is in the middle, and I apply the cautery as we have explained before, and apply the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn;
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if the patient is in pain and it's external, apply cauterization as I have instructed for those with paralysis and softening of the flesh, on the spine both at the back and neck, and use the olive cautery according to the method I have explained.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is young, make him a fine fire cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When it is due to melancholy that the excesses or moisture are corrupted and blood is thickened, then apply the cautery of partial cauteries as we have said for the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if it is due to the cause of melancholy that the excesses decline towards melancholy, and there are symptoms in the body of moist maladies, then let them drink something that purifies the brain according to what was stated previously in this section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After obtaining the head of the animal;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after making a linen thread well done, like a circle, if you place it around the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should lie in bed, and make sure they are well restrained from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	after applying the ointment, and using old burberry butter to spread it;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it on fire moderately, so that the patient can bear it or it can be handled;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after removing the circle from within through the head, and let it cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once a week each time with another effective method, until they recover completely.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or, if you see that it has been burned by making marks on almost the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain more so;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then place damp cotton in butter and fat from gelatine.
de l’awe des eulz	regarding the wisdom of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes first come by means of the signs that I have described in division, then you should start and continue to provide the patient with things that cleanse the head, and protect it from all moisture. Make them sweat or take several baths fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	After instructing to hold their head again, and have them cauterized while holding the head, and perform two cauterizations on the two temples when the pulse is descending in the head or at both eyes together, where one eye's pulse is descending into one;
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and apply all the cauterization to every vein and artery that is around the head, and have them cauterized long according to the width of the temples;
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and beware of blood clotting, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop it by pressing with part of your hand as you did.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incisions with cautery on how to apply it.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And whenever one applies the cautery or heated iron between the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	of the tears' boughs
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears of the eyes have become old and accustomed, and are located over veins or arteries that are in the outward appearance beneath the head.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	And you can see that they are cold, wet excesses, so I apply the cautery as I have said at the beginning of this treatment when descending to the eyes:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I apply the cautery at the top of the head, and two applications of the cautery on each temple, and two applications of heated iron between the two bones;
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	And if there is need for more, sear it carefully above the eyebrow with every small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the tears' paths within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you administer the remedies as we have discussed in the division, and if they do not benefit, then give to the patient three raw fowl soups;
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the reign of the head, and I have it cauterized or in the middle of the cauterization with olive oil;
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	And perform two cauterizations using the 'clavil' cauterization on the two eyebrows, a little above the hair.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and be careful not to cover the artery as you do this.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "claw":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then cauterize with this cautery which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	Of which the form is:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	And if you see that two cauterizations on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are;
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And do not let your hand rest until the third part of the paper is burned away, according to the method I have explained.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair which points the ear
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	Never has it happened that the hair of the nose turns into the nostril and reaches the inside; one does cauteries according to two methods:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	This means that either fire or burning medicine is used.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	With the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hair grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	And if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and become even, then put the patient in their healthy state;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	After drawing on the page about eyes, make a figure that is as such as the leaf of myrtle, and let it begin with the sign at the start of the hairs;
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Then I put moistened cotton with the yolk of egg and camphor of garlic on the eye, then warm up the cautery as shown here.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After that, apply the cautery to the figure you have drawn gradually and very little times, so that the heat is evenly distributed across it.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	And the signs of health in this operation are that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs stand at the angle of the eye;
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	Then lift your hand and let it be thus for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the scab is removed;
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the oil cure until it has become clean.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And when this comes to the hairs and the parchment has become soft, then resume the fire on that same place, just like you did at first;
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And when the hairs have departed, apply the cautery until the parchment rises to its natural place and remains even, not prickling the hairs with the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The burning medical cauterizers instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and even, then make parchment take on the shape of a bay leaf;
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	Then take French soap and fresh ashes, one of each, and grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	And make haste, so that it does not cool, then stretch upwards towards the shape you are made like a leaf of myrtle, and place the eyes on paper;
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	And if the illness lasts in this oil only, one must open in this way, and if it exists in both similarly;
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	And put over the oil cotton saturated with moisture, like an egg;
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	And the flesh of the disease be in your healthy part and place your hand on the medicine, and press on the spot several times whenever the disease feels the medicine's bite, because it feels the bite just like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, if the medicine prescribed to you is needed.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the bite has passed, lift up the limb from under, and reward if you see the paper lifted in the same way as it would be lifted by constraint of fire or by incision;
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And if this is the case, then do so well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	And if it's not this way, then reapply the medicine to its place or let the medicine take effect until your actions are equal and your eyes are focused;
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then place wet cotton with butter until the oil burns out, after which cleanse the area of the ointment known as "dyafenis" and others, until it is clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it's your business that you must guard well to your operation by great care so that no medicine leaks out from the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes oily and the hair catches in it, then apply the medicine to that part of the skin which is softened by the clean paper, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	After cleansing until it is clean.
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your restrictions;
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and do not let the right path be rejected by him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of treating fistulas by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have explained in the sections on diseases and your treatments are not beneficial, then it is necessary for you to apply a cautery treatment according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place their head in your healthy direction;
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and guide the guards of their head between your hands in such a manner that it does not move or let go of their head;
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after that, place cotton moistened like an egg or garlic juice on the eye;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	afterwards heat the cautery which is prepared:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and place it on the head as if it were the tip of a goose feather, ensuring that there is contact with the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	If you see it, if it points from one end to another, and if you see it, if it is also like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	However, this is what happens due to your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the fistula opens, and one treats the putrefaction, and dries it;
et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe;	And if it is closed, let it heal, and remove from the belly;
aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie;	After placing the fire cautery above it, hold your hand on the cautery near the part that is sensitive beneath the eye, so that your hands do not cause mischief;
et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	And place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the start of the cautery up to the bone, it would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;	If this doesn't work, then apply the fire cautery once more, and repeat if necessary, letting it sit for three days.
aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers;	After placing moist cotton and grease on it, continue the application of the ointment until it heals. If it does not heal within forty days, then apply an aqueous corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed.
et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	And observe the king according to what would come in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the old ones mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu;	Understand about fistula, and do as described;
aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	After placing in the incision a slender camel hair of this form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc;	and it is done to the amount of three parts of a spoon;
et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;	hold your hand or the camel hair firmly, and do not move the patient at all, so that the heat does not escape to their ear;
et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe:	And it is necessary to place on the eye of the patient cotton soaked with moisture or under wax:
li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	The plucking is done in the manner of the disease at its origin, and the healthy one through wondrous health maintenance.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery as we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	But if not, it is necessary to administer pertussis to the child and return the fistula to its proper place under the child's neck according to what is suitable in our own way.
des crevaices en levres	cuts in lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Rarely, there appear tears in lips which are called 'hair', and similarly in infants' lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these tears as we have discussed in sections, and if the treatment doesn't help, then apply this: take a small surgical instrument for cauterization according to this form:

aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the waxiness, while it is still healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule;	When it comes to the root of the throat or in the ovary, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after rotting and swelling and becoming inflamed, it turns into a fistula;
et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie:	And you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it yields nothing:
adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule;	So, it is necessary for you to have the cautery according to the size of the fistula;

dou movement des dens	The shifting of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain;	When the gums have softened due to moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine and if that does not work, then put the head of the bone back into its healthy position;
aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent;	After the heating of the cautery, its shape will come later in this manner that you place a stick under the tooth;
et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent;	And place inside the cautery until it heats up quickly, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth;
aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit;	After ease your hand and continue the cautery according to your will;
aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	After fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and keep it there for an hour and then remove it.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way, the teeth that were moving are stabilized, and the gums that were soft are made firm, and the moisture that was corrupt is dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When toothache comes from cold or if there is cold or fever, and the treatments of medicine don't help, then you need to use cautery according to two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	And butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	The wax cautery is such that you take tallow from a cow, and the tip in a spoon made of iron or spider.
aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez;	Take cotton and envelop it at the tip of a tent; in this place, moisten the wax with butter until it melts, then apply to the aching tooth as quickly as possible and hold until it cools down.
et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	And thus perform it often until the virtue reaches to the root of the tooth, and if you see wet wool and cotton cooled in the wax, apply it to the aching tooth, and place it on the heated iron until the fire reaches the warmth of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	The fire cautery is such that you take an iron or spider tail; make it large so that the flame does not reach to the base of the skin.
aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez;	After heating the cautery, from which its shape will come afterward, place it on the skin and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down.
fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Do this often, because the pain will be tolerable either that day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer;	And it's necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in anticipation of the cautery, and then press it firmly.
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir;	And apply the cautery according to how you desire and in accordance with what you can do;
et c’est li forme de la caine:	and this is the shape of the needle:
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie;	When the scrophules are due to cold wet and don't respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery as its shape will come afterward, and keep it open for two openings so that the vapors can exit from the other side of the cautery;

Li forme de la cainne:	The form of sugar:

de la mice	Of mice

de ydropisie	Of cautery with fire, command the patient to let the hair grow long and even; and if they prick at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	and have the cautery burns very close to the kidney's edge.

et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	And healing would hasten, and both intentions together with God's help will be united.

de plaie mal curee	of poorly treated wound

de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease

de la hainche	From the hip

de la dolor de la hainche	关于髋部的疼痛
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene:	When pain comes in the thigh area, it is due to cold and moisture, and the treatment prescribed earlier for this, if it doesn't work, indicates that the disease is old:
adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to cleanse the body of the large fluids using bad-scented pills or other similar good-smelling pills.
Aprés li fai cautere;	After this, perform the cautery;
et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres:	And the method of the cautery is according to two methods:
c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	This means "and it consists in assembling hot medicines, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz:	Fire cautery can be done in several ways, among which one is like this:
que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire;	You should apply the fire in an oblong area of the buttock, using three triangular cautery tools according to this shape, ensure they have good depth and size, place each tool with space equivalent to that of a coin between them, and use olive oil for these procedures;
aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Never apply the cautery in the middle of the buttock because there are four places according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche;	And if you see fit, apply the circular fire tool that we have mentioned in front regarding the dislocation of the buttock;
mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	But do it with care so that the circles contain all the hip, and all the points of the wound are cleaned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it's done in sciatica, when pain stays in the hip and doesn't reach up to the thigh or down to the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc;	And if it goes up to the thigh and leg, then apply two cauterizations there or where the patient says the pain is held, and one above the ankle three times, on the left side a little.
et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur;	And either use surgical cauterization or burn the wound's thickness;
et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if the patient feels that the pain extends down to two or three inches below the knee or near there, then apply cauterization where they feel the pain for three points or four at the cauterization called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus;	And if this requires it, do more;
et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the pain is near the knee towards the thigh, you should use a cutaneous or circular cautery on him. Make sure to take great care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave any remainder of the cautery and burn nerves and large arteries when you are using it. And don't cause the patient more harm and constriction with your actions.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen several who applied the cautery on the ankle bone, and it was effective until their legs swelled completely and likewise their feet were pierced and corrupted in all of them.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal treatment that led to death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are together in two parts, make a cautery on each one according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce;	And the wise said about the cautery of the hip, as follows: make it a piece of iron that is as thick as a small finger or perhaps a bit thinner, and ensure there are rows along its length with each row being spaced just enough to cover the area roughly equivalent to one inch.
et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait;	And let the rows be two-thirds in length, and let them also resemble knots, and have a well-made iron hook.
et c’est li forme:	And this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit;	And when heated, keep it until it is thoroughly red and steaming, then place it over the buttock of the ailment, and twist it towards the healthy side;
et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors;	and once burned after the fire has been applied and it is left for three days;

aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the ointment cure until it is healthy.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent;	Albucus says that we use little of this cautery for the fear of his judgement, and few see fit to use it;
et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	yet this is one of the better cauteries, which can be tolerated, and where it becomes necessary.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi;	The burning medical instruments for use are such that you make an implement with intertwining parts into which the edge of the door descends. et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	and let them extend forward and upwards, and join together in this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche;	After placing the thigh bone on the lying patient's healthy side at the hip joint, and press your hand very near to the thigh bone;
