The other body parts, such as the limbs and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder blade and back spine and ribs and arms and legs, and similar seeming limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerves or arteries and it's not poisonous, like what I will tell you, this happened to me because of what you were doing.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow hit him near the neck at its base:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and pulled it out from the other side beneath the ear's fat, and was perfectly fine afterwards.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And pulled out an arrow that had hit into the fat near one eye beneath the eyelid, and the arrow was found to be completely inside, only its tip could be seen towards the shaft, and it was an arrow as large as a Turkish bowstring, but without harming any nerves.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The body was healthy, and no harmful accidents befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he removed an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was from Arabia to the ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I tended to the wounds, pricked them as finely as possible while I was extracting the arrow, and made all Christians well.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And he removed an arrow from someone's house, that it was stuck in the chest or stomach, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then having passed 30 days, if it did not change its condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut at the arrow, pulled it out, and forced it, and there was no bad incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you find an arrow has fallen or stuck to the back of someone's house, and made the wound heal from there;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And the arrow stays within, not finding any harm in any of its natural works, nor adapting to its natural dispositions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man who was hit in the face by an arrow, and they缝ed up his wound;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and he endured this without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and no other symptoms.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And one day he was hit by an arrow in the home of the princes' king, who had been shot in his neck, and he was leaning slightly to the right;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was fully inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for treatment after it had been three days since they were hit.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried to get close to everything with a subtle attempt, yet I felt nothing.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he complained of pain and discomfort in his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was due to the tip of the arrow. I placed a therapeutic adhesive plaster on his head because his ears were not inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And my suspicion about the ear was confirmed by it.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I had the plaster on for several days and quickly resolved the wound. The patient endured this long enough until he felt the arrow inside his nose;
et il le me dist.	And he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied corrosive anti-fever medicine to the wound for several days until it was opened, I tried it and felt the tip of the arrow that was buried in his head;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then adjust by using that medical remedy for the opening of the wound, until I clearly see the head of the arrow.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and puncture well the ends for about three months, and then widen it as much as I can with my forceps, from both sides, and it couldn't come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I didn't stop refining and engineering tools for the creation of instruments, until I obtained one day with well-made forceps, according to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, until I used it, and kept the wound open.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the judges determine that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	So I kept it open, and healed the wound completely, and fully recovered the patient.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	You were told about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you place your treatment where I do not specify, because the books cannot take everything into account;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare well to little more than a few things, and on what is current and lacking, find nine works, and nine tools, in the removal of foreign objects that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows are stuck into limbs according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the entry point or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And when it enters by the wound or where it enters, the arrow penetrates into the flesh, and this has happened no other times now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't spring up now, let it grow until the flesh is well rotted internally, and becomes free from disease.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And also if it's embedded in the bone and cannot come out, let her stay like that for several days, and remove a little each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it will spring up, and if it doesn't, pierce internally with all the delicate force until the veins are widened inside, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and extends up to one of the brain's chambers, or any of the incidents I've mentioned occur within the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you do not remove it, but let her stay until the wound is even after several days, because if the arrow reaches up to this point, it's a fatal situation.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not go up to the sinus, and remains without any bad event for several days, then one should use a device for extracting it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is firmly stuck like this and cannot come out force, then apply ointments internally, as I have told you;
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area until it becomes healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if an arrow has been inserted inside the body and we can't see it, then look everywhere for it;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then try to guide it with any suitable tool;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot follow it due to the tightness of the wound or the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then cut as much as necessary for the wound to be open;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	And pull the arrow if you can, and if it has ears on which it rests in the arrow, remove the flesh that is stuck from both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And handle it carefully so you do not break the arrow, but pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it in one go, till your arm is numb from the effort, then move on, because the extraction requires endurance.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding causes you difficulty, then apply what we have said about treatment in our chapter concerning this.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and beware of cutting near the nerve and vein, and do it carefully so that you can remove the arrow without risk, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and guide the patient according to how they were before the arrow fell, because that is the greatest help for them, and if you cannot do so, then follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that came from another side, or if there appears to be no injury at all, or if the skin is swollen in the place where you see it or feel it differently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Therefore raise up high, as long as the forceps can take hold, and then proceed:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as she enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull her out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, let her stay in place, and then start the extraction again until she jumps out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is an arrow that has been shot, if it hits the whole body;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is in the lung, and you see that it is necessary to force it out, if you use the correct tool, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the handle of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then force it, and if the arrow is buried, you force the instrument with its pointed end inside, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touching, it is necessary that you remove all the flesh around where I come in, if possible, then treat the wound as is fit.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is lodged or pierced in the chest or in the abdomen or in the bladder or in the rib area, and it's close to vital organs, you should only press up there, if you press down.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and protect against pressing the artery and nerve, then you extract it, and then suture the wound; this is a task for expertise.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used for extracting arrows resemble a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways in this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	Large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead resembles the feathers of a bird, for it is pointed like the tip of an arrow; thus it looks like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs for shooting and retrieving is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common horns
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins through which we bleed, of which there are or from which there is a head of 16, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	Two smaller ones located behind the ears, which are called "two grasses";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in the two visible temples;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called "apparitors";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is within the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that's at the nose bridge on the head;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are in the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these veins are called "augueherich";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins by which we commonly cleanse are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the Cephalic type, and it's situated on the left side of the chest, and they call this 'the man of the head'.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	And the middle one is called 'the fast', and it's made up of the cephalic type and the basilic type, and they call this 'a vein for the heart'.
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And the basilic is either on the right or left side of the chest, and they call this 'a vein for the belly', and it's located near the axilla, and it's the one that's bled from, which opens clearly in the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the basilic is the vein that's located between the little finger and ring finger, and it has two courses;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	One is below the curve of the left chest pocket, and the other is in the ankle of the right side of the body.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein that's called "nasse", which is located in the ankle of the other side of the body;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg, there are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The cleanliness of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old plagues and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of a surgeon, like what I've told you, and when you laugh at the head of an illness and touch the body or areas with veins with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then squeeze the patient's neck like winding a thread, until you see the two veins behind the ears in two loops under the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Guide your hand there, and where you feel the pulse at your neck, noble sir of the wound;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and press it down along the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand all the way up to the vein above, cut through both skin and vein carefully as they should pass each other, and let blood flow out until you see it.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then squeeze and tie, until the wound is clean;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have explained the incisions and the cautery in this first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The cure for the two arteries that are in the two temples, requires ancient grain intake and rest, and systematic eye exercises, and treatment of cold tears from the eyes;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of a surgeon are thus as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and when the patient stretches his neck, so that both veins can be seen clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels for the pulse all over your body, and then speaks of examination;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then gently raises the hand over the vein at your second finger's tip, and holds the scalpel nearby, then raises the vein at that point, and starts the incision, just as you did in other veins earlier, and perform the bleeding according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then frees the patient, place your second finger on the vein for an hour, then put it on cotton;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then forms the cut, leaving it open until it heals;
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And we have spoken of them regarding their development and extraction, or at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment for the vein in the forehead is just as important as that of the temporal vein when dealing with diseases affecting the scalp, and it includes migraine, and fever.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is such that the patient twists her neck, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the tool called "drill", as shown below:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, and let blood flow according to how much you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then relieve the patient's neck and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and without any cuts, where the work of the surgeon should be with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Otherwise, it is not right that the flames become too fierce;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the wound goes across, for the bone is close by, and by chance the flames might break the bone when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The treatment of the two veins that are in the two eyelids helps with the eyes, at the nose, and on the cheeks, and in the ear canal when it comes to the ear, and for diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of its treatment is that the patient tightens their throat by twisting some string, as previously.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then apply the treatment, and let the application go across, somewhat in line with the length of the flame, somewhat wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if their flames are subtle, by chance they might break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	Then drain the blood as much as you need to, and then tie it with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The treatment of the vein near the nose is valued for fever and colds, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	And the quality of this treatment is that the patient constricts their throat, then pinches their nose with their left hand, and take hold of the subtle flame long, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well like that, and the bleeding will now start to drain;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And don't go too long without food, and adjust to your need the flow of blood, then leave for a night, as she is very quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and it's the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the lungs helps in tightening the alvine, and in the beginning of syphilis, and for many diseases, and in pneumonia, and corrosion, and in herpes, and tuberculosis;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of health is such that patients restrain their throat from one side to the other, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	And may the masters be on the edge of the patient's throat, and the patients sit at the edge, then heal the vein for a long slightly wider part, then guide the blood moderately, or as much is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	Then redo another part in the other vein, then untie this knot, and hold back moderately the veins, so as not to strangle the patient.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it be until morning, that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	In the art of healing wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The treatment of veins above the lips helps in closing them in the mouth, and it deals with gum decay, cracks in the lips, nosebleeds, and tooth pain.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of healing is to have the patient stand in front of you, and hold his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	Then turn the lip, and look at two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and you know them by what they are black, and by what in their vicinity there are small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	So pinch both, and if you don't know them and are in doubt, then pinch the largest of each part, and do similarly with the two veins above and below, for it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	In the healing of wounds under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of veins that are below the tongue requires help after the healing of the cephalic region, and this is in constriction of the throat, and in diseases of the sclera, and in diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of the surgeon is such that when you squeeze the wounds between your hands in front of the sun and lift the tongue, and look under each side, you find a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore heal both of them and do not overdo it, because there lies the arteries under them.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the chest that we commonly heal are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by piercing with any large incandescent flame, or with an olive-smooth one like the blade of a trencher, and it is called "anevil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are broad and fine according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the fire brand Mirtin is greatly renowned, and it is quite wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it takes skill to open thick knotted veins full of visible large blood, and those containing large blood and disturbance;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and it is the shape of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it's more subtle and pointed, and it's for purifying the delicate veins, or having subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The blood from the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that occur in the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the surgeon to heal correctly, and he must be aware of the artery that is nearby.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding occurs, it is necessary to stop the bleeding, just as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And must never grasp the flame, but cut it as before.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica does not open clearly, then it is necessary for you to extract it, and use another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or if you want no blood from it, or you open the vein instead of it with your arm:
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cut is done with the flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know where to cut, it is necessary for you to pull the arm so that you touch the place as long as you can feel the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark where to cut, and then bind the arm, and cut the vein with the flame as we have said;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And remember not to cut into the artery when you see the limb swelling up, for it is from the artery:
eschui la donques.	Therefore, here it is.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulging up high like the urine of a child, and the veins are red and delicate, know that this is blood from the artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, and place your hand for a while, then press firmly until the vein stops bleeding, which has happened many times;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Hold his arm, and leave it like this, and do not move your patient;
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And lie on their back, and do not move them until they have cooled down.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the vein has not stopped bleeding and it takes too long, and you lack medication, if you cannot close the artery when it opens, for its head is withdrawn;
et estainche li sans.	And stop bleeding the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take an elm bark, and cut it, and take one of the halves and bind it well until the other joint.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	When the wound stops bleeding, that is enough;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If not, then treat it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the stopping of the bleeding is not done with many preparations for the small size of the wound and the strength of the connection of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The healing of the vein in the middle helps treat bleeding from above and below the elbow, because it is made up of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it befits the surgeon that they should beware of the nerve which is nearby, and if he does not go too far forward, and he finds the nerve, and it swells and harms the health, and by chance cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any person due to its subtlety, it befits you to have the instrument sterilized before use;
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And listen to the nerve with your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two hands, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The surgeon in the treatment of the cranial region helps, relieving blood flow to the head, and aids with eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it befits the surgeon to intervene in the olive oil vein or in the arm vein, for this is the safest of all veins, as it has neither nearby nerve nor artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Always, strive for the lightest touch, and do not fret if you have to try it first time, and then repeat if necessary;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance, the limb might swell in some people when done for the first time, but there's no harm if you do it again.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about surgery is that it's not performed merely for health preservation and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and so, if the surgery is done in one of the three veins, namely:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	That's to say, frontal, facial, and basilar;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should perform surgery at the beginning of prayers while kneeling, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	And one must cleanse on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The treatment for diseases does not have a set time period, but rather depends on the need of the day or the body, at all hours and in every situation;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not proper to cleanse children up until they are twelve years old, nor pregnant women for only a quarter of their term up until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Neither should they heal the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when one desires to be cleansed, in whatever manner, it is necessary for them to perform mild bowel irrigation, if they have retained feces, so that the veins do not attract excesses from the intestines that harm the main limbs;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor is one cleansed by those who are overly bloated with meats, or drunk to the point of being incapacitated, whether due to excess strength or those with dehydration;
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if warned by the physician after colic pain, and vomiting, and abdominal distress, and frequent need to relieve oneself in women, and labor pains, of staying awake and working, and whatever saps the strength, or from something due to weapons or injuries;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the humors within you, if they are too abundant due to meats and beverages and medications; use your judgement for their intake.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then take a bath or plunge, if nothing is lost in the process; this will help refine the blood and cleanse your veins of the belly's waste products, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And keep this day free from work, pain, and excess, and any similar activities;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	And be mindful of your diet and exercise moderation. Ensure the physician stays higher than the part being treated, and rub the arms twice or three times. Gently massage the bandage afterwards; if it is too tight or loose, it cannot properly contain the blood flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with hands, until the veins swell, and when felt.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	Then moisten the wick of a small piece of old oil flame, then place his left hand's finger on that vein right under the area being treated for just a moment where he intends to apply heat, so that the vein doesn't burn and break upon contact with the metal.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that behave like strings when heated, and some are filled with air currents, in such a way that when placed over the flame, they pull away from the flame and fail to open up, and thus belong to those types.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it causes the vein to constrict, then the wound is too narrow for this; so that the flame must be aware of such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the body endures this first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if not, try again slightly around that area or at an acceleration, as long as the limb isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the body starts to anticipate pain, let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	By chance, there may come pus-filled blisters;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Don't take baths, then start cleaning it if it suits her;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the wound is small or the vein is too thin and you doubt whether it's leaking as much blood as you see, pierce that very spot directly into the entire flame;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	And the work proceeds somewhat hastily, so that the arms are swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	For this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see that the arm is inflamed, do not start anew with healing, and place a bit of oil on it instead, for oil lightens the body from blood, and heals there where oil is applied.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And administer the oil to every healing you do on veins, so as to stop the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And in the same way vinegar and wine help when applied to the arm;
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If it is too large, refine the veins and spread them out.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if it comes about that there's an abscess large in size, which happens many times, especially when the wound is not fully healed even once or twice at the time of opening the vein, then hurry up, and place a damp sponge on top with some hot water and a little oil, then hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And you should do this after the discharge of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place for several days without any blackness or greenness, then it does not harm him;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see any sign of it, place something made from aloes or myrrh in a concoction of chamomile, mint, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there would be pus and appearance at the healing of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Place your hand there, and if you find the elbow soft under pressure from your hand, this is an appearance of malady.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	So listen, do not apply anything from what we have spoken of, for perhaps in this there is no connection to the artery;
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but make it slightly damp to harden the elbow, then treat with another cure, until it heals properly.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each person with blood according to the amount of their virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the wound is black, let pus flow out as long as it remains red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it swollen, let it drain until it becomes thin.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it's too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it's necessary for the full and healthy individual who needs blood extraction to make a wider incision and let the flames be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it suits him well to clean often and gently, and you must clean him by cutting across, not straight.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of cleaning saves from the spreading of blood and constriction of nerves, and is better than long cleaning over width.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And for the one whose body needs cleansing, it's suitable to give him moist bread made from juice of pomegranates;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If he is flushed, let him drink three or four times of blood. If he has a cold complexion, have him eat something before the cleansing that's moist bread in syrup, or syrup with aromatic honey and spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cardamom, and the syrup should smell very good.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it fails in surgery, after the issue of a little blood, it should inhale soup of flesh, and pleasant subtle syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on collapse, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if they wish to bleed their arm, and then rest again, should this be necessary, when it has been weakened by much bleeding, it should be bled little by little, according to the strength of its power continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if someone wishes to bleed their arm after the first bleeding, and they have strong health, they should be bled seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if someone wishes to undergo bleeding on another part of their body, they should be bled on the second day or the third day at the latest.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, causing fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	If so, it requires large quantities to be drained, and widen the incision until it pierces the heart;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	Then when you have fulfilled all the conditions of health, and place your hand on his heart when it is healing, so that death does not come from the heart rather than the lung, this happens many times, when the surgeons are careless;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not good when you see the arm being released and blood being expelled a second time, and the incision is closed, so you press firmly on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	Nor if he has curved it, to extend the arm quickly, for that would be badly done;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	But let it grow until it heals for the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	but when you apply it at the tip of the flame, until the frozen skin starts to melt from the heat, and place on a damp cloth in hot water, then gently press.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and don't squeeze it, until the abscess is relieved.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if needing to bleed again for blood, if the health is in that place itself, or in another vein, or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein exists in the arm just like the one by the head because it is made up similarly.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is such that the injured person holds their hand in hot water until the pulse turns red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it moderately, so that the vein can be seen clearly, then heal now through it, neither too wide nor too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and if the cut is too wide, heal well near the wrist joint, and if blood cannot flow out, then place the hand in hot water, let the blood drain into the water, as long as you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it's in this state, do not reset the hand into hot water, as you would put it more at risk of frostbite than in heat;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the healing of this vein is more certain than for all other veins, as it contains neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of regaining the right hand is worth more than any illness of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Stretch the hand, and reset it in hot water until the vein is visible, if you can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the healing is across, and if you press all over it without causing any pain;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	And do not press too hard, for the nerve is completely bare of flesh everywhere, and then put the hand in hot water, if it's frozen in the wound and can't escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is required of you, place on the vein where and with a needle to solder quickly, and thus do for each rain.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The health of the left hand is to the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you regarding the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The healing of the sinew affects all diseases that are within the body, such as diseases of the liver, and blockage of fluids, and diseases of kidneys, and of old hands and feet, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its health is such that the patient bathes their feet in hot water, and rubs on the wound until it heals, and applies this to the joint at the ankle.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And when the wound is on the ankle, then above their foot many drops of rain occur;
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So heal it properly or even more extensively, whether it's on the ankle, as long as you can move it freely.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it on the foot, be aware of the nerves that are nearby, and heal across in the same way as when peeling.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and may the flames extinguish quickly.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot come out without causing harm, then put the bone in water and ensure that the vein is well emptied.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it needs to be healed once, then try the second time starting slightly above, because the skin is salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and similarly perform surgery on the other side equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the sciatic nerve are at the ankle joint on the side, and its health corresponds to hip pain, when it's due to internal bleeding.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of its health is such that it allows the patient to bathe in water and exercise on the ankle, turning four times by twisting, because otherwise the vein will not be accessible;
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	And if it opens, heal her in all possible ways and when crossing over;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better if you hold her down because the leg muscles are strong and she responds well to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find it, heal no part of what opens or at the back of the foot, and toward the small toe, and guard against nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And make such correction of the blood as you see fit, and then untie the knot, and place a cotton bandage and tighten it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	The treatment has now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Of suction healings
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Pessaries are made from horns, or spiders, or worms;
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and cupping is performed in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	either by piercing and drawing blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this cupping that involves piercing can be done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	either it is with instantaneous heat, or without heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And cupping that involves piercing and the extraction of blood is done in four quarters of a man's body, where one is completely solid.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the other is around the neck;
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and the other two in each side of the neck;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And the suction cup under the chin;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	And the suction cup on both shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the suction cup over the pimple;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	And the suction cups on both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	And the suction cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	And the suction cups on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And suction therapy does not address large blood vessels that are scattered throughout the body, for it would weaken one if done so, just as we perform bloodletting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor at any hot or without heat, in any disease caused by excess, until all the bodies are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if suction is necessary due to diseases, or by habit, we should administer it every hour at the beginning of her period, or at the end, and throughout and in each phase;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to suction, if they do not rest often;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and for those who experience swelling and heat in their face, and head, and neck, and the eyes appear dark to them;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who notice a drop of blood in their mouth, and have an extended tongue, and cough up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are those who think, see through the nose blood and ashes and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the first month, we instruct people to take some air after three hours of fasting each day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The health of the nose helps with inflammation of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of all over the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this process of drawing out evil spirits, if it is to be done in the health treatment for the head, should not be used by those with cold constitution or who have fever, because it causes much harm to them.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason, one should not use it if they have health issues related to cold conditions or cold nature.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And the one who often seeks cleanliness, becomes forgetful, and because of this, it is necessary to place the suction cup a bit further down due to the element of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The process of ventosation in the neck is part of head health care and basilica treatment. For this reason, it is valued for its impact on the foot and for cutting the channel of the heart lung, as well as generally, and for refilling;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should be applied gently, as if it is held too tightly, it may cause paralysis or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventosations at the two ribs of the neck are good for head pains, eye problems and toothaches, and for strangulation, as well as pain in the root of teeth, being part of basilica healthcare.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is necessary that you instruct the surgeon to prepare his hand for surgery, not to cut the artery and avoid any spurts of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The breaths under the chin if they lead to mouth diseases, and gum decay, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth;
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is related to the health of the inner lining of the lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The breathing around the shoulders leads to illness caused by heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The breaths around the elbows are as significant as the three major veins of the arms, for they carry blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And instruct the surgeon not to cut too close, for the muscles are bare of flesh and touch near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The suction cup placed on the back is related to kidney disorders and illnesses nearby; it must be large and made of skin so that it can properly treat.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And by chance, if she were subtle, she would break;
et i fai grans plaies.	and I cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The leg cups are applied firmly, because they draw blood from the entire body, and are effective against old abdominal pains, menstruation pains, and bladder issues, and relieve swellings;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and are located on the two shins and the two ankles, and moreover they weaken the body after long use, and cause pallor in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you apply it first in a vacuum state, and maintain continuous suction, applying it quickly, moving evenly, and continuously doing this until you see the area turning red and swelling, noticing the heat from the blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Afterwards, and replace the suction cups, and be cautious in the placement of the horns, for there are those who have thick flesh, and clear pores:
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	It is necessary to cut only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a bit deep.
et suce legierement.	And suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the animal is large, it may be necessary to cut twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to subtilize the blood path that is thick.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the animal is very fatty, it may be necessary to cut a third time;
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we wish to milk slowly and gradually from the blood vessel, we only apply it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, then we often renew the application;
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the wound is deep, so severe and piercing that it immediately pierces the veins, this technique is suitable for those with thick skin and hardness, who have endured much pain. You should grease their wounds with suckers that open and dissolve when applied.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it's in purple fat or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it's in fat (of an animal), use mustard oil, or rosemary oil, or chamomile oil, or any similar kind.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of arnica, or balsam, or juniper oil, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is in need of strengthening and has large swellings, no oil should be applied; it's better to wash after suction with pink water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or any similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And whoever has much moisture, if they rise from rest, or from water of myrtle, and from sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And for those who have large excesses, they rise from old wine or vinegar, or from the distillation of juniper or chamomile, or other similar substances;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	And they should not be treated with suction cups before or during the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And do not sleep after suction, it is necessary that he take care, when he should be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch over him who is being treated and is hot-tempered, and if he is too active and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	It is necessary for him to eat cold things, such as pomegranates, endives and lettuces in broth, and similar items;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And eat fowl, and beef stew, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those with a cold constitution, they should eat honey syrup and fragrant half-aged wine, which is between old and new, and eat small portions, and fowl stew, and small birds such as pigeons;
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day he gets suctioned, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it should be given to some people no garlic or muskmelon before suction, or after, to strengthen the main limbs;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And you should sieve the water, but it is not good for those who are cold to drink them.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are placed to hurt are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and in gout, and on the stomach and intestines and kidneys, and buttocks. For this member does not suffer being hurt with needles, and it is only done forcefully to draw blood from limb to limb, as when we place them on the nipples when the child cannot suck;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to thin out the viscosity in the limb, as when we place suction cups on the stomach and intestines to reduce the limbs;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And for pain when there is an obstruction or stone, so by its attractive power it may adhere to the obstruction, or evacuate the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And thus she acts when you place her above the heart and under the belly in cases of retained wind, and these suction cups are administered empty to remove such wind only;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with hot water, as in illnesses causing colic, and in such manner one fills the suction cup with boiling hot water, or with water that has cooked suitable herbs for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should have half a palm wide and deep halfway down, with its edges at the midpoint one small notch, as to pierce like a needle, made of brass so that it doesn't cause the patient pain when placed on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And in the middle there is a rod crossing like an arachnid or iron, for to hold a candle, and it should be large and small according to the illnesses and age of those who use them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups for children are different from those for adults, and the thin ones are different from the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this suction cup like this on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take the wax candle or the cotton thread, and place it inside the suction cup through the rod that is in the suction cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup to not burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the limb, and you should do this at the part as we have said, so that when one wants to, if there is vapor going up, remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And take the thread path as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup then, which is administered in the disease of pleuresin, for all colds, there is no pus nor discharge, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and placed solely on the limb;
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Without utensils, they are administered only in limbs where suction cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in their naked flesh, like buttocks or cheeks, and other similar areas;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and as for the quality of applying suction, if you find without utensils that are in mild water without pus, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And place them in sweet water, until they become familiar, and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then bleed and use suction cups, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place it on stones;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they're full and start to bleed, if it's possible to place suction cups, do so, because this is not much after.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the limb from the bed and then water, very well, and then incise;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the limb bleeds too much after the use of cups, moisten it with a linen cloth in cold water and place it there, until the cups are cool.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are multiple cups, place them on powdered vitriol or garlic and similar things, until they cool.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	You place half of peeled hazelnuts inside the limb, and let them dry there until they are now sealed off.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more, take other walnuts instead.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if walnuts cannot be quickly obtained, rub the limb with fresh blood, or stick an awl there until blood flows out, then place them on top. Soon after they sense the blood, they will dry;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are excreting, sprinkle a little aloes and ground grain or ash powder on them, and they will start healing now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with the restoration and healing of fractures.
