Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, you young man who looks at this chapter, that they have never seen any of the old books or read a letter about it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this reason, the knowledge has been extracted from our land, for I have never found any good;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, for through the knowledge of old books, which I studied so much that I dealt with this knowledge, and through experimentation, and through the habit of my life;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	And in this chapter, I have described what is contained here and summarized it at the end, clearly showing the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in those two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to outline the essence of this book in its introduction and prologue, and highlight the chapters where wise minds apply their intellect. We should adhere to truth, so that those who have been taught can understand and learn this noble art, and teach it to others as well.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I state that when any fracture or dislocation or twists or bruises occur in no part of the body, it is necessary for you to quickly cleanse the patient on both sides, if nothing weighs them down, such as weakness, children, or elderly people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	If the tightening is too tight, or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and cook with cold broth, which means chilled soups, and onions and parsley, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and make sure the dish is not too full of foods that fill the veins with blood until you have no doubt of an abscess or the spreading of material in the body;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient's condition improves as per their initial regimen, as they have used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that cause heavy digestion or are viscous, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and leeks, and peas, and cow liver, and eggs, and fresh fish, and heavy wine, and similar items.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at any time of loosening they are moved more quickly and quicker is the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones of the elderly and those in decline cannot be healed or joined well according to their nature due to the drying out of the limbs, nor can such bones which are too tender, like those of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	But if there is no cure, reset it at the broken bone on the large tendon that stretches out and joins the limb together, until you force it as it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And do not finish his work entirely, and for this it is necessary to nourish with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breakage of the head is different from the breakage of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you all manners of breaking in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the elbow, and others through prodding, such as the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a broken bone with an injury, or a break resulting in a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each has his own means and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory comes to his mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that the breaking of the bone occurs when his ear is twisted, and opens well below, and is squeezed by the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twist and the ear is not pierced, and the patient does not feel much pain, if there is no breaking;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it can well have twisting, or cracking, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it doesn't suit you to move it with your hand, but apply the remedies that follow, and then gently strain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break which happened at the shoulder, and it has two parts separated, they now need to be put in equal alignment, so as to have abscesses lie straight or run.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if the pus-filled abscess is drained, if he leaves no day, until the abscesses become calm;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	Then apply it evenly as you can lightly and wisely, know that the restoration of this is easier than restoring those with pieces;
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then compress it, as it should be done as described hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, and it is divided into two parts, whether they are bones or wood, or under your hand if it's a small member, or divided by two strings, or with one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the limb according to its natural shape, so when the parts of the injured member are healed, you can realign it through every effort by moving them as much as possible, and make sure that in your actions no injury or pain befalls the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And feel it well in your hand if you think it is not properly done:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	If it's done beautifully, and you don't pull it too much, not pressing as those who make the abscess swell and cause muscle tension do in their own way, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is ready, carefully guard over the patient so they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, when turning or in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And make sure the limb is so securely placed that no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	And when there is no pain being felt, it means that it isn't in the right position, and one must place it in such an arrangement that no pain is felt.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and see to it that it is placed correctly, so that there is no distortion when restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the quality of the broken limb matches what I'm telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken vary in size and extent, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are smaller limbs such as arms and legs, etc.:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	and it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are larger, such as the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	If it is necessary to encase with a wide and hard band, for wide bands embrace the whole large limb, and restrain equally from all sides, so that there is no difference;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then bind around with light straps, three times or four according to the limb, and hold your hand slightly on every band, then go above the breakage and restrain less there, so that the breakage may be moved a little upwards.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the band gradually and gradually, until you reach a large part of his healthy limb, then take another band and return around him towards the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the breakage and restrain moderately, neither too hard nor too gently, as we have said in the first instruction above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Place between the linen loops or pieces of cloth, as long as they are all even, then tie everything over with a bow, and then place your well-made stars on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place on something that soothes the abscess and removes the swelling, letting it stay like this for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then tighten over your stars, and they should be half the width of a tightly wound rope or bamboo stalks, or from what is used to make darts, and they should look like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	However, it's necessary that the star placed on the break be slightly larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	And let it be as long as is necessary for the size or largeness of the limb;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold onto the pins just like you did in the first instance, then add a strip of fabric above it, similarly to what was done in the first instance on the burn wound;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	The constriction becomes tighter over time, gradually reducing.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	And it is necessary for the thread to be of medium size, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is thick, like those that farmers use to tie their linen ropes in their work, and this is a great mistake, because the tying cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it does not suit for there to be less than two fingers' width between each pin.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patients are sore from the nails of the stakes after the tightening at their healthy parts, then put patches of linen or shoddy wool on them, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is inflamed and the joints are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not right to constrain all limbs broken on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it does not suit to use pins straightaway, but rather after five or seven days, or more depending on the severity of each successive abscess.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	And here is the way of old plastering methods to restore fractures, dislocations, and twisting:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And take flour that remains in the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of eggs, and prepare this concoction, neither too thin nor too thick. Use it, and this is the common method of plaster restoration for various types of damage, as well as women and small children, because it does not cause harm whether it's too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method for restoring plaster to fractures, dislocations, and twisting:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take ginger, onion, garlic, and asafetida, and gum Arabic, mix them with water equal to three parts of the total weight of these ingredients;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	And myrrh and aloes, mix them with five parts of water;
alechil VIIII З.;	The number seven;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	And make it into powder, and mix it with the yolk of an egg;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	If the condition of the patient is hot, then use this plaster, for it has a good composition, and heals broken bones quickly, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another way of using the plaster that is beneficial for dislocations:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take milk and vinegar, use in proportion of ten to one;
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mix myrrh and aloes, use the ratio nine to three;
acaice VI З.;	Use six parts of sugar;
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Take ten parts of Armenian balm, grind it well, and mix with water or the yolk of an egg, then administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to treat joints and fractures is by setting them back into their places, and alleviating the pain that follows, and they cut down the bone, and apply pressure.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new one, and mix it with honey and oil that has been cooked, then place it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Plastering does not heal completely, but it is better for soothing abscesses and properly treats bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another way to set bones which breaks bones back into place:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and leaves of terrestrial mulberry, grind them together, then make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the restoration of bone breakage and to soothe the removal of pus.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take root of balm, chamomile, flowers of violets, meal from cloves, one part of each;
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	And grind it with wine, and apply the mixture to heated limbs, or mix it with moist parsley water, or water alone, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plastering more firmly than the first when an abscess is returning to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take roots of valerian, and seed of flax, rush, marigold, and wormwood, and flowers of violet and chamomile, from each take a portion;
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind it with the strength of salt water, or sweet cold water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates states that to restore strength in a fractured limb one should apply a salve made of beeswax and oil, and nothing else more. He says it should be between two layers neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that we should place upon the broken limb for restoration, things slightly moistened but somewhat warm, such as mirr (mastic), aloe, incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method for plastering that is useful in injuries and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take the gall and kidneys of disemboweled men, or bird feathers, valerian, and an equal part of saffron, and grind them together, make a plaster from it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then remove the plaster slightly later, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is there movement of the bone in its place;
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If not by hand for days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itchiness, without rest or swelling, should you feel urgency, and dislocate it, and set the plaster now;
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a moist sea sponge, and dip it in water, and cool the limb, until the itch stops, and pain is soothed;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it with a bandage until you are sure of removing heat.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and let the inflammation settle in the limb, and sooth the pain, then resume gentle movement, and a little plaster, do not strain it as much as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And precisely when it is healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus and redness, pain and swelling are subsiding, indicating the injury has healed throughout, then you need plaster and bandaging; start again as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said happens to the limb, or if it is not released until after three, four, five, or seven days;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And leave it for twenty days, as we see fit, until the fracture heals and brings about an adjustment of the flesh;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	Then increase the restriction beyond the first stage, allowing for growth of its flesh, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	And if you see the limb drying more than it should, know that there will be no improvement;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Bathe it with hot water afterwards, every time you release it, and let this happen each third day, and scrape a little of the joint;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	Through this work then cut into the flesh of the limb, and quickly follow what the foolish surgeon does, that leaves the member deformed:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is bad, and if it's full of pus-filled boils, I only see one way to do it: leave the cuts straight and open them properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and their causes are specific;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	because there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the elbow bone hits all the way to the joint that is below the bone, similar to how a mallet or staff might cause damage;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	And because of this, this kind of fracture is called 'mallet injury'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or the sword hits the bone from above without piercing it, and this kind of fracture is called 'absolute'.
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	And these are the injuries from these two fractures, large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack in the bone, or injury from stone, or impact on stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break that approaches until it reaches the tissue beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound is healed in the bone as finely as a hair, and the crack is small, because of this it is called this "hairline" fracture;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound is made either by piercing through stone or falling or from something similar, and the piece of bone enters below, so that it is split in the middle like a candle when it has burned through the candles.
si entre li piere dedens.	And if within the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more in those with moist bones below, such as children's bones;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	And occurs through all these ways of fracture that result in small fragments like splinters.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breakages through the diminishment above them, and the examination at stakes, and by the corrupt flesh which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair can be recognized when one has exposed the bone and rubs it inside, revealing the black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating breakage, beware of adverse effects due to malaise, and if you do not encounter any bad side effects such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stretching, pallor, fever ague, and other symptoms appearing in various conditions, it cannot be cured without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming mishap, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when winter comes first to you, and if it is winter, then it's necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is spring, then you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, in such a way that the pus around the bone is rotten, and accidents occur as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the breakage of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to cut the broken part in this way:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and when you touch the unripe head of the patient, and expose through the bone in every way that you can, and on the shape of the wound as much as you can, and if blood leakage occurs during exposure of the bone or pus appears, then use what is necessary, and when you fill the cavity with moistened cloths in olive oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the pus subsides and there is assurance of blood flow;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin digging into the bone, and this is done according to two ways of operation:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is to cut closely at the front, and this is its shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have several different sizes of cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron indelibly;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And work lightly, so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is firm and hard, it must be pierced internally, so as to apply cuts with needles instead of directly, not piercing through the bone beyond the testicle, and there should be a margin or circle above the tip that does not allow the tip to pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	And it must have several (needles), so that each grows into its place of the thickness of the bone, and you will have needles for all testicles;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And this is the form of the three ways of cuts:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality of piercing inside the broken bone is that you place the cut on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	Then place another cut somewhere slightly later on, and thus do this all around. Then scrape in the space of the bone that is between the teeth, and do this more subtly than you can, gently, as we said, until you pull the bone to your hand, or to none of the instruments you have such as forceps;
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	And make sure not to touch the brain or the sinuses.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, if it is necessary that you finish off the edge of the bone left from the os to all other instruments like a tooth, but it must be more robust and more delicate than the other tooth;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if it remains with no small bones, nor any scales, if the bones are lightly struck with instruments;
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with bandages and applications that we have discussed.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another way of treatment is what Galen said, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the oath very strong, and it's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover a part of the bone where the fracture opens and moves. So when you have uncovered that part, place underneath the tip of this ophthalmic incisor, as described here:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And don't cut from one side only, and the injury is divided into two sides, so that cutting faces towards bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	Then strike with a small mallet there, so that you gently hit the bone all around, and be well aware of the thread that is nearby;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is close to the bone, then gently hit the bone because hitting the bone causes no harm and no fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce until the cloth and only cuts through from above, with small pieces remaining, then after that roughness, use a fine razor to remove the scales. You must have various quantities of this tool in order to administer the most suitable treatment for each location according to the manual and the appearance of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you stand before great razors, and after finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other hair trimming cuts and delicate breakages, you must apply your skill according to its direction;
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this matter is not answered by the one who has dedicated their studies in this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if it is revealed to be pus, then you must apply linen bandages according to the size of the wound, and mix with a little rose oil, and place it on the wound;
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another bandage doubled in two or three layers, and soak it with wine and rose oil, then place it on the first bandage;
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	And do this as lightly as possible so you don't burden the pus, then administer another layer of bandage above it, but do not apply too much force until only the wound is dampened;
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	And let it be so for one or two days until the abscesses are somewhat calmed, then displace it and give medications like root extracts of this, cornmeal, incense powder, and sage, as well as similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And make a powder from these and put it on the wound, then give appropriate medications without causing irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And see that the wound is clean, do not leave any ointment on it and do not allow the scabs to stick together. For when scabs stick together on the brain tissue's mesh, they can move about and cause great harm to the patient;
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And when you place something corrosive over it, it eats through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, so that no harmful events occur to the patient as we have said, in case there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if fear does not leave you only because of the medicine we have placed on it, and this virtue exists, then you should take part of honey and three parts of rose oil and one drachm of glue, and place this mixture under your tongue;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply the appropriate curing methods until they are cured, when it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Know that neither of the two parts above the nose are ever broken, or just one by itself, for these are two bones;
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And that below is cartilaginous and does not break, neither can it be twisted or bent, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must pinch your little finger or under the nose, and make the break equal in the tip of your ring finger, then by rubbing through the middle, as long as the nose regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain through your operation.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose part and cannot reach to its place at the head, then it is necessary that you make it equal to the tip of a stick somewhat thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is two parts, redo another piece, and strive to restore the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or tenth day when the abscess is subdued, then apply to the head under the nose with strips of linen bandage, and if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you hammer on another side, if the break is there;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	And let them be large enough to fill out the hollows under the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no healer should grease the nipples with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I don't think this is quite right, but they should be moistened in the preparation of a mixture with egg and powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilage has hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And no later than once or twice use goose feathers instead of tents, and if the bird's body swells inward, and there is a stinging sensation, then let the wind blow through them;
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	just do whatever you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose in the same way as you are doing it, then put a poultice or wet cotton in oil mixed with it, or in one corner of a spoonful of snail juice.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if pus forms and doesn't go away, apply a poultice outside, made of ground myrrh and powdered frankincense, mixed with yolk from an egg. Then place it on light bandages, but don't tie the goose's neck;
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the cuts on the nose are small and the bones have broken into small pieces, use tools suitable for this task, then clean out through the incisions with things that cause purging, and then seal it back up, using poultices or ointments that are suitable for this purpose;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the nose, treat it with a poultice, and place a wick in it, as long as it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken externally, and there's no wound outwardly, only the fracture is external. It isn't broken into two halves completely; rather it breaks internally as well, which can be discerned lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the breakage is in the right side, that you bend your ring finger towards the mouth of the wound;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	And if the breakage is in the left jawbone, then bend your ring finger of the right hand, and gently place the break inside, and work it out on the other side by the exterior, and apply evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is a break in both parts of the jawbone, it must be treated with extension of half parts, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if tooth movements or rupture occur, then stretch it with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then place on the broken jaw plaster, and set upon the two cloths;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place on the cloth a well-made wide board, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the jaw, and fasten it at as many points as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you notice that the shape changes, dislocate it on the third day, and then set it back to the position where it changed.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And place plaster on it, mixing the powder from the mill with enough egg or flour of almond meal after you have removed the wax.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	And place on the plaster a soft wool, and if the plaster hardens and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it until they are well;
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Many times, one is well in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if pus-filled ulcers come about, then apply what we have repeatedly instructed.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is both fracture and wound together, remove any piece of bone that has broken out.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	If the extraction requires delicate tools suitable for this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there is nothing left, if the wound is wide, place one plaster over it suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it heals.
de la forcele	with strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The forces break multiple times before reaching the shoulder, towards it, and the breaking happens according to three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	Or she is broken and drained in two parts, with fragments, and it's the more lightweight one to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Or there is breaking with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the operations occur when breaking is felt through the wound, when you have two helpers, so that one marks the shoulder where the force is broken;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends down along the neck to the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	Then place the break evenly on your thumbs, so that the shape is as it should be, and there's no appearance or strain.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend more, place a round sponge under the shoulder for the patient, of cloth or wool, and its size should be according to your necessity;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And they make it slightly weak, hold the spear to your hand so that you can apply an even break, as is proper.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head from the strength's force behind it, because it comes forward, then the patient must lie with their head resting on their pillow, and place one of the shoulder's cushions under both shoulders. Have the attendants press the shoulder downwards until the bone of the strength rises.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And address the break to your fingers, and if you find weak spots, it is right that you split through there;
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	And pull the parts gently, and if the bone cannot join despite any exertion, it is to be cut at one of the incisions you have made;
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but make sure you have a firm grip on that instrument, to withstand that tension:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and make it resemble a spoon, not too thick, and be as wide as it should be according to the size of the bone and the strength of the task;
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and have two heads, as you see, and make one wide, and the other thin, as is the wound you made when treating the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of the location of the abscess, if you cut the wound, and if its rupture is small, or if you doubt about the location of the abscess, if you treat the wound with bandages and tents, according to their quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And when the abscesses are drained, if it is moist, soak bandages in oil rose and in sweat and wine, and place them on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The grinding of the bone, when it is concerning wounds and surgery, consists in applying a plaster made from the powder from a mill and some butter of an egg onto the bone. Place light pincers on top, and put a sponge underneath if needed;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large band about the size of a palm wide, then place two layers of bandages on top of the pincers and plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take an elastic strip about three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the tip of the bone is hanging down.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	And place the iron above the wound, and turn the bendstick towards the neck, and across the healthy elbow, and across the diseased elbow;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	And reset each part individually. When you see that the heat keeps the wound steady near the break, and you clearly see that the iron doesn't move over the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when you remove the ligaments, then you hold it in place;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	And let the malady discharge on its back, and place him when he sleeps with a small pillow under his elbow, to raise the shoulder up;
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If it reduces the strain of the muscles by adjusting the position of the shoulder, or you tie his arm to the neck, and do not release him from this injury until no bad accidents occur for 20 days;
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then reapply the plaster if you see it is needed, and hold it in place without moving it until it has healed.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And it usually takes up to 28 days, or sometimes less time for recovery.
de la brisure de l’espaule	From the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Sometimes the shoulder breaks or is injured at its end or in the middle, and it's damaged only due to impact;
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	If you align it according to the break's shape, and reset it according to its natural form, in all ways that you can;
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	Then apply flour ground in the mill with plenty of eggs, and gently rub it in, then place a double layer of cloth on top;
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place a broad and slender bolster under it, somewhat wider than the shoulder, and ensure there are no movements anywhere on the shoulder; if there is hair or linen strands, position them so that the bolster sits evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	And then he restrains it tightly for quite some time, so that the limb does not move from its place, and he checks the connection each day;
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	And each time he pulls it back, if he restrains, and puts the limb on par with where it was originally, should it be at its place, and lies the patient on their side;
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	And the shoulder is restored in 20 days or in 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when this number is completed, if it dislocates again, be sure, for it's not an os that will put itself back lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment is ahead and not at the corner, then do it above, and the wound will open again. Then, follow what we have said about treating bleeding abscesses.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is broken once in the middle, but this happens rarely;
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken at the middle, if the arm is lowered and there is great pain felt by the patient, and lack of circulation, all over the body, and sometimes vomiting blood occurs, and cuts open in the broken bone, and one can feel this well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And in the restoration stage if the body lies with its back and hips on the ground, then place I under his shoulders, press the shoulders down, and assemble the ribs of the second ribcage with your hands. Carefully adjust them to be equal across all manners that you can perform, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place them on the plaster and wrap them with the subtle pile of salt, or another light substance, and cover it with a cloak. Fasten it onto the broken bone so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and twist the banding round on the back, and tighten it in correspondence, and reward each hour the ligature, and if it relaxes, then tighten it;
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it seems to be untying due to corrosion or itching that comes to the body, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and untie it, remove the plaster, and treat in ways of treatment for what has come upon them.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove the plaster, and hold it until it is sound.
de la brisure des costes	from the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaking of ribs only occurs after a large hit on the back and within it, and they bend only because they are brittle;
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	And one feels this well during examination at the testicles.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And for the repair, you should make the break equal, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bind it with one strap if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of ribs occurs within, one feels great pain and sharp pain, as well as crying out, like in childbirth, because the bone pierces the skin;
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And it causes pain points, all over and vomiting large amounts of blood, and this is a sick health, and the old ones had to endure great suffering.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say it is necessary to consume meat that inflates the belly, in order to expel wind from within.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not follow this, that pus and sulfur should be introduced if it has not already been there.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has already been there, then heal it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And it was said that one should put suction cups on the body to drain fluid, for this is in line with reason;
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt as to whether the suction cup attracts excesses towards the head due to the condition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And it is said that when one must cover the body with wet wool in heated oil, and to place cloths between the ribs to make the wound equal inside, then follow the treatment of bleeding, of meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patient feels intense pain that cannot be borne by the bone piercing through the skin, there is doubt for the patient, whether it's necessary to cut towards his head from the place of the broken rib, and it's advisable to use tools under the pectoral muscle to prevent further collapse;
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then one must cut the bone, treat it lightly, and then stitch the two edges of the wound if it's large, and dress it with plasters until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if pus comes out, put wet cloths in oil and place them on the wound;
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And treat while the wound is as it should be for pus, and always place remedies on the ribs where it needs to be, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No break occurs to the bones of the neck, and no bending is caused;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	And similarly in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to any person, and you wish to determine if they will heal or not, watch carefully whether their hands are softened and swollen and dead, and cannot be moved or extended, and when you prick them with a needle, if they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that death can occur in various circumstances, and if they do not move well when held back and forward, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the disease has been cured, if care is applied to it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if such a thing happens in the spine of the back, you should know whether it is healthy or not. et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when it occurs on his belly, an involuntary emission happens.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is observed on its back and it wants to rise, if it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Know that these are fatal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if no care is taken in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this misfortune does not happen to him, then it is a matter of less concern.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment consists in giving care if there is an abscess to drain, if you apply oil on the spine or on the spot of blood or of the yolk of egg, until it soothes;
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then place on one of the soothing plaster, drying ones, and tie it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest;
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.

et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And set the bone, then join together the two edges of the wound if it's large, with stitches. Then treat with ointment until healed;
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone head is broken, which they call "the bone of the knee", then squeeze your pouch from your left hand, and place it evenly against the other hand at your power, then apply the plaster and the poultice on top, if you need to.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then it is held, and if there are broken bones, they are lifted up, and the bone is set, and the wound is treated until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the breaking of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It happens that the hip bone is broken, and if it happens, if there's a bit of discomfort in the head;
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And stretches for a long time, and descends into the pubis, and comes with pain in the head, and bruising, and inflames what is broken.

et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	Know which is the break and its alignment;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the break is only in the head, set it evenly to that break, as long as it's in its natural alignment.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Regarding the breaking of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The shoulders are those that lie between the blade and the top of the shoulder, and if they are broken, you should restore them according to one of two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Do this: take a rod of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	And bind them with two straps, and place them on top, and seat the patient on the position;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	Then let his broken arms rest on the rod, until it reaches under the armpit, and has made a bend equal to the length of the rod, then place him on anything heavy or have them lower him down;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place the broken part evenly under both hands until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method is that you fix the skin on his neck, and tie the hand to the neck, then command two attendants that one of them shaves the one above the wound with their hands, and the other cuts down to all half an inch, and extend each in their respective parts.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more severe, then hold tight to the thread around the bruising, and above the bruising, and extend each of the ministers to their share.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the broken part is close to the shoulder joint, you should place one strap under the armpit and the other towards the elbow, under the break.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And similarly if the breakage occurs towards the blade, then it is necessary to place the thread lightly, without effort, until the breakage is even on the surface and on the blade;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then equalize the breakage, as necessary, and apply pressure, if pus does not come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if pus does come out, then do not apply pressure until the seventh day, and place on wet wool and oil rose for as long as the pus is relieved;
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	Then apply pressure. The method of applying pressure involves placing the plaster over the breakage and then aligning the arm with the shoulder, and putting your hand on the shoulder or near the breast;
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and apply the bandage, and hold it with the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its natural position, if no object impedes or if the bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use these methods, and place one bale on the fracture larger and stronger than others, with two inches between each bale, and ensure that every bale is large enough to pass three inches from both sides;
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then apply pressure to the bales as I instructed at the start of this chapter on fractures, forcefully but not too much when spreading them apart.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the setting of the bales and the compression, as we have explained, when you are restoring the broken limb, and if there's any doubt about the abscess, leave it to be bound until seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	Then look at each three days the bandage, so that no itching appears or spreads to the area, or there won't be pus formation coming into the limb because it's too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such events occur, should the dislocation not be corrected until three days or more have passed, and let the patient rest on their back, having their hands on their stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place underneath the shoulder a cushion evenly filled with hair, and observe every hour of the day or night, whether the shape of the broken limb does not move or if the joints are softened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if it is treated with the aid of medicine, and give them the meat that we have prepared in front, in such a way that the meat becomes first refined;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when it begins to increase, if it becomes large.

et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And then one must release it and apply baths and remedies of ointments for the ease of the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is ugly and tangled, it should be left for loosening for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is made of two bones, which are called the pair "foscile", from which one is smaller, and it is this that supports the pit.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	And the other is large, and this one is underneath, towards the small two;
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	By chance only the large "foscile" breaks, or the small one, and by chance they come together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small "foscile" breaks, the restoration is light, and the healing;
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large ones break, the healing is bad, and more painful than when they break together.

Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it's large swelling, then you must restrain it more forcefully;

puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the servants' arms to the part under their hand, or at the elbow, and another servant on the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the eyes evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if during the breaking into pieces, you place each back in its original position, and if none of them is broken to be grasped by the hand, and you cannot restore it to its original position, then you do work on and the bone, as we said before.

soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	So if the pain is in one of the bones, or in two;

Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the connection after some days.

et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the limb not be forced to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then continue the reduction, and if the ligaments have been torn and the bones exposed, and resembling a thing, perform it.

And if precaution is taken so that no distresses cannot come to the limb because it is too constricted, it should be that you soften it with pox (a kind of compress or poultice), and leave it in this manner for a few days, until the distresses have passed, and then you should tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, or the release does not happen until after twenty days.

de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and around our thumbs there are few breaks, and only bending happens many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the hand is broken or bent at its joints, it should be treated with a warm application, and held straightly in front of them equally;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then place his hand on the extended table and extend the attendant's broken bones, and set them equally straight, until they are properly joined together;
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And place the dressing and splints, if no abscess forms, then he applies an ointment according to the size of the wound;
